<a name="5.2.7">Here in this city visiting the sick,</a><br>
<a name="5.2.8">And finding him, the searchers of the town,</a><br>
<a name="5.2.9">Suspecting that we both were in a house</a><br>
<a name="5.2.10">Where the infectious pestilence did reign,</a><br>
<a name="5.2.11">Seal'd up the doors, and would not let us forth;</a><br>
<a name="5.2.12">So that my speed to Mantua there was stay'd.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech4"><b>FRIAR LAURENCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.2.13">Who bare my letter, then, to Romeo?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech5"><b>FRIAR JOHN</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.2.14">I could not send it,--here it is again,--</a><br>
<a name="5.2.15">Nor get a messenger to bring it thee,</a><br>
<a name="5.2.16">So fearful were they of infection.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech6"><b>FRIAR LAURENCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.2.17">Unhappy fortune! by my brotherhood,</a><br>
<a name="5.2.18">The letter was not nice but full of charge</a><br>
<a name="5.2.19">Of dear import, and the neglecting it</a><br>
<a name="5.2.20">May do much danger. Friar John, go hence;</a><br>
<a name="5.2.21">Get me an iron crow, and bring it straight</a><br>
<a name="5.2.22">Unto my cell.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech7"><b>FRIAR JOHN</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.2.23">Brother, I'll go and bring it thee.</a><br>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech8"><b>FRIAR LAURENCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.2.24">Now must I to the monument alone;</a><br>
<a name="5.2.25">Within three hours will fair Juliet wake:</a><br>
<a name="5.2.26">She will beshrew me much that Romeo</a><br>
<a name="5.2.27">Hath had no notice of these accidents;</a><br>
<a name="5.2.28">But I will write again to Mantua,</a><br>
<a name="5.2.29">And keep her at my cell till Romeo come;</a><br>
<a name="5.2.30">Poor living corse, closed in a dead man's tomb!</a><br>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE III. A churchyard; in it a tomb belonging to the Capulets.</h3>
<p></p><blockquote>
<i>Enter PARIS, and his Page bearing flowers and a torch</i>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech1"><b>PARIS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.1">Give me thy torch, boy: hence, and stand aloof:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.2">Yet put it out, for I would not be seen.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.3">Under yond yew-trees lay thee all along,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.4">Holding thine ear close to the hollow ground;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.5">So shall no foot upon the churchyard tread,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.6">Being loose, unfirm, with digging up of graves,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.7">But thou shalt hear it: whistle then to me,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.8">As signal that thou hear'st something approach.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.9">Give me those flowers. Do as I bid thee, go.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech2"><b>PAGE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.10">[Aside]  I am almost afraid to stand alone</a><br>
<a name="5.3.11">Here in the churchyard; yet I will adventure.</a><br>
<p><i>Retires</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech3"><b>PARIS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.12">Sweet flower, with flowers thy bridal bed I strew,--</a><br>
<a name="5.3.13">O woe! thy canopy is dust and stones;--</a><br>
<a name="5.3.14">Which with sweet water nightly I will dew,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.15">Or, wanting that, with tears distill'd by moans:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.16">The obsequies that I for thee will keep</a><br>
<a name="5.3.17">Nightly shall be to strew thy grave and weep.</a><br>
<p><i>The Page whistles</i></p>
<a name="5.3.18">The boy gives warning something doth approach.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.19">What cursed foot wanders this way to-night,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.20">To cross my obsequies and true love's rite?</a><br>
<a name="5.3.21">What with a torch! muffle me, night, awhile.</a><br>
<p><i>Retires</i></p>
<p><i>Enter ROMEO and BALTHASAR, with a torch, mattock,  &amp; c</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech4"><b>ROMEO</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.22">Give me that mattock and the wrenching iron.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.23">Hold, take this letter; early in the morning</a><br>
<a name="5.3.24">See thou deliver it to my lord and father.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.25">Give me the light: upon thy life, I charge thee,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.26">Whate'er thou hear'st or seest, stand all aloof,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.27">And do not interrupt me in my course.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.28">Why I descend into this bed of death,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.29">Is partly to behold my lady's face;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.30">But chiefly to take thence from her dead finger</a><br>
<a name="5.3.31">A precious ring, a ring that I must use</a><br>
<a name="5.3.32">In dear employment: therefore hence, be gone:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.33">But if thou, jealous, dost return to pry</a><br>
<a name="5.3.34">In what I further shall intend to do,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.35">By heaven, I will tear thee joint by joint</a><br>
<a name="5.3.36">And strew this hungry churchyard with thy limbs:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.37">The time and my intents are savage-wild,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.38">More fierce and more inexorable far</a><br>
<a name="5.3.39">Than empty tigers or the roaring sea.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech5"><b>BALTHASAR</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.40">I will be gone, sir, and not trouble you.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech6"><b>ROMEO</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.41">So shalt thou show me friendship. Take thou that:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.42">Live, and be prosperous: and farewell, good fellow.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech7"><b>BALTHASAR</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.43">[Aside]  For all this same, I'll hide me hereabout:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.44">His looks I fear, and his intents I doubt.</a><br>
<p><i>Retires</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech8"><b>ROMEO</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.45">Thou detestable maw, thou womb of death,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.46">Gorged with the dearest morsel of the earth,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.47">Thus I enforce thy rotten jaws to open,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.48">And, in despite, I'll cram thee with more food!</a><br>
<p><i>Opens the tomb</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech9"><b>PARIS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.49">This is that banish'd haughty Montague,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.50">That murder'd my love's cousin, with which grief,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.51">It is supposed, the fair creature died;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.52">And here is come to do some villanous shame</a><br>
<a name="5.3.53">To the dead bodies: I will apprehend him.</a><br>
<p><i>Comes forward</i></p>
<a name="5.3.54">Stop thy unhallow'd toil, vile Montague!</a><br>
<a name="5.3.55">Can vengeance be pursued further than death?</a><br>
<a name="5.3.56">Condemned villain, I do apprehend thee:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.57">Obey, and go with me; for thou must die.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech10"><b>ROMEO</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.58">I must indeed; and therefore came I hither.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.59">Good gentle youth, tempt not a desperate man;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.60">Fly hence, and leave me: think upon these gone;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.61">Let them affright thee. I beseech thee, youth,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.62">Put not another sin upon my head,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.63">By urging me to fury: O, be gone!</a><br>
<a name="5.3.64">By heaven, I love thee better than myself;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.65">For I come hither arm'd against myself:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.66">Stay not, be gone; live, and hereafter say,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.67">A madman's mercy bade thee run away.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech11"><b>PARIS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.68">I do defy thy conjurations,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.69">And apprehend thee for a felon here.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech12"><b>ROMEO</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.70">Wilt thou provoke me? then have at thee, boy!</a><br>
<p><i>They fight</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech13"><b>PAGE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.71">O Lord, they fight! I will go call the watch.</a><br>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech14"><b>PARIS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.72">O, I am slain!</a><br>
<p><i>Falls</i></p>
<a name="5.3.73">If thou be merciful,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.74">Open the tomb, lay me with Juliet.</a><br>
<p><i>Dies</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech15"><b>ROMEO</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.75">In faith, I will. Let me peruse this face.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.76">Mercutio's kinsman, noble County Paris!</a><br>
<a name="5.3.77">What said my man, when my betossed soul</a><br>
<a name="5.3.78">Did not attend him as we rode? I think</a><br>
<a name="5.3.79">He told me Paris should have married Juliet:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.80">Said he not so? or did I dream it so?</a><br>
<a name="5.3.81">Or am I mad, hearing him talk of Juliet,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.82">To think it was so? O, give me thy hand,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.83">One writ with me in sour misfortune's book!</a><br>
<a name="5.3.84">I'll bury thee in a triumphant grave;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.85">A grave? O no! a lantern, slaughter'd youth,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.86">For here lies Juliet, and her beauty makes</a><br>
<a name="5.3.87">This vault a feasting presence full of light.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.88">Death, lie thou there, by a dead man interr'd.</a><br>
<p><i>Laying PARIS in the tomb</i></p>
<a name="5.3.89">How oft when men are at the point of death</a><br>
<a name="5.3.90">Have they been merry! which their keepers call</a><br>
<a name="5.3.91">A lightning before death: O, how may I</a><br>
<a name="5.3.92">Call this a lightning? O my love! my wife!</a><br>
<a name="5.3.93">Death, that hath suck'd the honey of thy breath,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.94">Hath had no power yet upon thy beauty:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.95">Thou art not conquer'd; beauty's ensign yet</a><br>
<a name="5.3.96">Is crimson in thy lips and in thy cheeks,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.97">And death's pale flag is not advanced there.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.98">Tybalt, liest thou there in thy bloody sheet?</a><br>
<a name="5.3.99">O, what more favour can I do to thee,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.100">Than with that hand that cut thy youth in twain</a><br>
<a name="5.3.101">To sunder his that was thine enemy?</a><br>
<a name="5.3.102">Forgive me, cousin! Ah, dear Juliet,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.103">Why art thou yet so fair? shall I believe</a><br>
<a name="5.3.104">That unsubstantial death is amorous,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.105">And that the lean abhorred monster keeps</a><br>
<a name="5.3.106">Thee here in dark to be his paramour?</a><br>
<a name="5.3.107">For fear of that, I still will stay with thee;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.108">And never from this palace of dim night</a><br>
<a name="5.3.109">Depart again: here, here will I remain</a><br>
<a name="5.3.110">With worms that are thy chamber-maids; O, here</a><br>
<a name="5.3.111">Will I set up my everlasting rest,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.112">And shake the yoke of inauspicious stars</a><br>
<a name="5.3.113">From this world-wearied flesh. Eyes, look your last!</a><br>
<a name="5.3.114">Arms, take your last embrace! and, lips, O you</a><br>
<a name="5.3.115">The doors of breath, seal with a righteous kiss</a><br>
<a name="5.3.116">A dateless bargain to engrossing death!</a><br>
<a name="5.3.117">Come, bitter conduct, come, unsavoury guide!</a><br>
<a name="5.3.118">Thou desperate pilot, now at once run on</a><br>
<a name="5.3.119">The dashing rocks thy sea-sick weary bark!</a><br>
<a name="5.3.120">Here's to my love!</a><br>
<p><i>Drinks</i></p>
<a name="5.3.121">O true apothecary!</a><br>
<a name="5.3.122">Thy drugs are quick. Thus with a kiss I die.</a><br>
<p><i>Dies</i></p>
<p><i>Enter, at the other end of the churchyard, FRIAR LAURENCE, with a lantern, crow, and spade</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech16"><b>FRIAR LAURENCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.123">Saint Francis be my speed! how oft to-night</a><br>
<a name="5.3.124">Have my old feet stumbled at graves! Who's there?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech17"><b>BALTHASAR</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.125">Here's one, a friend, and one that knows you well.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech18"><b>FRIAR LAURENCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.126">Bliss be upon you! Tell me, good my friend,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.127">What torch is yond, that vainly lends his light</a><br>
<a name="5.3.128">To grubs and eyeless skulls? as I discern,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.129">It burneth in the Capel's monument.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech19"><b>BALTHASAR</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.130">It doth so, holy sir; and there's my master,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.131">One that you love.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech20"><b>FRIAR LAURENCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.132">                  Who is it?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech21"><b>BALTHASAR</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.133">Romeo.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech22"><b>FRIAR LAURENCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.134">How long hath he been there?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech23"><b>BALTHASAR</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.135">Full half an hour.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech24"><b>FRIAR LAURENCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.136">Go with me to the vault.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech25"><b>BALTHASAR</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.137">I dare not, sir</a><br>
<a name="5.3.138">My master knows not but I am gone hence;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.139">And fearfully did menace me with death,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.140">If I did stay to look on his intents.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech26"><b>FRIAR LAURENCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.141">Stay, then; I'll go alone. Fear comes upon me:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.142">O, much I fear some ill unlucky thing.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech27"><b>BALTHASAR</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.143">As I did sleep under this yew-tree here,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.144">I dreamt my master and another fought,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.145">And that my master slew him.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech28"><b>FRIAR LAURENCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.146">Romeo!</a><br>
<p><i>Advances</i></p>
<a name="5.3.147">Alack, alack, what blood is this, which stains</a><br>
<a name="5.3.148">The stony entrance of this sepulchre?</a><br>
<a name="5.3.149">What mean these masterless and gory swords</a><br>
<a name="5.3.150">To lie discolour'd by this place of peace?</a><br>
<p><i>Enters the tomb</i></p>
<a name="5.3.151">Romeo! O, pale! Who else? what, Paris too?</a><br>
<a name="5.3.152">And steep'd in blood? Ah, what an unkind hour</a><br>
<a name="5.3.153">Is guilty of this lamentable chance!</a><br>
<a name="5.3.154">The lady stirs.</a><br>
<p><i>JULIET wakes</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech29"><b>JULIET</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.155">O comfortable friar! where is my lord?</a><br>
<a name="5.3.156">I do remember well where I should be,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.157">And there I am. Where is my Romeo?</a><br>
<p><i>Noise within</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech30"><b>FRIAR LAURENCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.158">I hear some noise. Lady, come from that nest</a><br>
<a name="5.3.159">Of death, contagion, and unnatural sleep:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.160">A greater power than we can contradict</a><br>
<a name="5.3.161">Hath thwarted our intents. Come, come away.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.162">Thy husband in thy bosom there lies dead;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.163">And Paris too. Come, I'll dispose of thee</a><br>
<a name="5.3.164">Among a sisterhood of holy nuns:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.165">Stay not to question, for the watch is coming;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.166">Come, go, good Juliet,</a><br>
<p><i>Noise again</i></p>
<a name="5.3.167">I dare no longer stay.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech31"><b>JULIET</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.168">Go, get thee hence, for I will not away.</a><br>
<p><i>Exit FRIAR LAURENCE</i></p>
<a name="5.3.169">What's here? a cup, closed in my true love's hand?</a><br>
<a name="5.3.170">Poison, I see, hath been his timeless end:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.171">O churl! drunk all, and left no friendly drop</a><br>
<a name="5.3.172">To help me after? I will kiss thy lips;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.173">Haply some poison yet doth hang on them,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.174">To make die with a restorative.</a><br>
<p><i>Kisses him</i></p>
<a name="5.3.175">Thy lips are warm.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech32"><b>First Watchman</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.176">[Within]  Lead, boy: which way?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech33"><b>JULIET</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.177">Yea, noise? then I'll be brief. O happy dagger!</a><br>
<p><i>Snatching ROMEO's dagger</i></p>
<a name="5.3.178">This is thy sheath;</a><br>
<p><i>Stabs herself</i></p>
<a name="5.3.179">there rust, and let me die.</a><br>
<p><i>Falls on ROMEO's body, and dies</i></p>
<p><i>Enter Watch, with the Page of PARIS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech34"><b>PAGE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.180">This is the place; there, where the torch doth burn.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech35"><b>First Watchman</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.181">The ground is bloody; search about the churchyard:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.182">Go, some of you, whoe'er you find attach.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.183">Pitiful sight! here lies the county slain,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.184">And Juliet bleeding, warm, and newly dead,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.185">Who here hath lain these two days buried.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.186">Go, tell the prince: run to the Capulets:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.187">Raise up the Montagues: some others search:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.188">We see the ground whereon these woes do lie;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.189">But the true ground of all these piteous woes</a><br>
<a name="5.3.190">We cannot without circumstance descry.</a><br>
<p><i>Re-enter some of the Watch, with BALTHASAR</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech36"><b>Second Watchman</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.191">Here's Romeo's man; we found him in the churchyard.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech37"><b>First Watchman</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.192">Hold him in safety, till the prince come hither.</a><br>
<p><i>Re-enter others of the Watch, with FRIAR LAURENCE</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech38"><b>Third Watchman</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.193">Here is a friar, that trembles, sighs and weeps:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.194">We took this mattock and this spade from him,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.195">As he was coming from this churchyard side.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech39"><b>First Watchman</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.196">A great suspicion: stay the friar too.</a><br>
<p><i>Enter the PRINCE and Attendants</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech40"><b>PRINCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.197">What misadventure is so early up,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.198">That calls our person from our morning's rest?</a><br>
<p><i>Enter CAPULET, LADY CAPULET, and others</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech41"><b>CAPULET</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.199">What should it be, that they so shriek abroad?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech42"><b>LADY CAPULET</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.200">The people in the street cry Romeo,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.201">Some Juliet, and some Paris; and all run,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.202">With open outcry toward our monument.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech43"><b>PRINCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.203">What fear is this which startles in our ears?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech44"><b>First Watchman</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.204">Sovereign, here lies the County Paris slain;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.205">And Romeo dead; and Juliet, dead before,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.206">Warm and new kill'd.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech45"><b>PRINCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.207">Search, seek, and know how this foul murder comes.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech46"><b>First Watchman</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.208">Here is a friar, and slaughter'd Romeo's man;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.209">With instruments upon them, fit to open</a><br>
<a name="5.3.210">These dead men's tombs.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech47"><b>CAPULET</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.211">O heavens! O wife, look how our daughter bleeds!</a><br>
<a name="5.3.212">This dagger hath mista'en--for, lo, his house</a><br>
<a name="5.3.213">Is empty on the back of Montague,--</a><br>
<a name="5.3.214">And it mis-sheathed in my daughter's bosom!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech48"><b>LADY CAPULET</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.215">O me! this sight of death is as a bell,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.216">That warns my old age to a sepulchre.</a><br>
<p><i>Enter MONTAGUE and others</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech49"><b>PRINCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.217">Come, Montague; for thou art early up,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.218">To see thy son and heir more early down.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech50"><b>MONTAGUE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.219">Alas, my liege, my wife is dead to-night;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.220">Grief of my son's exile hath stopp'd her breath:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.221">What further woe conspires against mine age?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech51"><b>PRINCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.222">Look, and thou shalt see.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech52"><b>MONTAGUE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.223">O thou untaught! what manners is in this?</a><br>
<a name="5.3.224">To press before thy father to a grave?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech53"><b>PRINCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.225">Seal up the mouth of outrage for a while,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.226">Till we can clear these ambiguities,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.227">And know their spring, their head, their</a><br>
<a name="5.3.228">true descent;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.229">And then will I be general of your woes,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.230">And lead you even to death: meantime forbear,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.231">And let mischance be slave to patience.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.232">Bring forth the parties of suspicion.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech54"><b>FRIAR LAURENCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.233">I am the greatest, able to do least,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.234">Yet most suspected, as the time and place</a><br>
<a name="5.3.235">Doth make against me of this direful murder;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.236">And here I stand, both to impeach and purge</a><br>
<a name="5.3.237">Myself condemned and myself excused.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech55"><b>PRINCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.238">Then say at once what thou dost know in this.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech56"><b>FRIAR LAURENCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.239">I will be brief, for my short date of breath</a><br>
<a name="5.3.240">Is not so long as is a tedious tale.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.241">Romeo, there dead, was husband to that Juliet;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.242">And she, there dead, that Romeo's faithful wife:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.243">I married them; and their stol'n marriage-day</a><br>
<a name="5.3.244">Was Tybalt's dooms-day, whose untimely death</a><br>
<a name="5.3.245">Banish'd the new-made bridegroom from the city,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.246">For whom, and not for Tybalt, Juliet pined.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.247">You, to remove that siege of grief from her,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.248">Betroth'd and would have married her perforce</a><br>
<a name="5.3.249">To County Paris: then comes she to me,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.250">And, with wild looks, bid me devise some mean</a><br>
<a name="5.3.251">To rid her from this second marriage,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.252">Or in my cell there would she kill herself.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.253">Then gave I her, so tutor'd by my art,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.254">A sleeping potion; which so took effect</a><br>
<a name="5.3.255">As I intended, for it wrought on her</a><br>
<a name="5.3.256">The form of death: meantime I writ to Romeo,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.257">That he should hither come as this dire night,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.258">To help to take her from her borrow'd grave,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.259">Being the time the potion's force should cease.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.260">But he which bore my letter, Friar John,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.261">Was stay'd by accident, and yesternight</a><br>
<a name="5.3.262">Return'd my letter back. Then all alone</a><br>
<a name="5.3.263">At the prefixed hour of her waking,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.264">Came I to take her from her kindred's vault;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.265">Meaning to keep her closely at my cell,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.266">Till I conveniently could send to Romeo:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.267">But when I came, some minute ere the time</a><br>
<a name="5.3.268">Of her awaking, here untimely lay</a><br>
<a name="5.3.269">The noble Paris and true Romeo dead.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.270">She wakes; and I entreated her come forth,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.271">And bear this work of heaven with patience:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.272">But then a noise did scare me from the tomb;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.273">And she, too desperate, would not go with me,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.274">But, as it seems, did violence on herself.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.275">All this I know; and to the marriage</a><br>
<a name="5.3.276">Her nurse is privy: and, if aught in this</a><br>
<a name="5.3.277">Miscarried by my fault, let my old life</a><br>
<a name="5.3.278">Be sacrificed, some hour before his time,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.279">Unto the rigour of severest law.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech57"><b>PRINCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.280">We still have known thee for a holy man.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.281">Where's Romeo's man? what can he say in this?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech58"><b>BALTHASAR</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.282">I brought my master news of Juliet's death;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.283">And then in post he came from Mantua</a><br>
<a name="5.3.284">To this same place, to this same monument.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.285">This letter he early bid me give his father,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.286">And threatened me with death, going in the vault,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.287">I departed not and left him there.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech59"><b>PRINCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.288">Give me the letter; I will look on it.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.289">Where is the county's page, that raised the watch?</a><br>
<a name="5.3.290">Sirrah, what made your master in this place?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech60"><b>PAGE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.291">He came with flowers to strew his lady's grave;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.292">And bid me stand aloof, and so I did:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.293">Anon comes one with light to ope the tomb;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.294">And by and by my master drew on him;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.295">And then I ran away to call the watch.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech61"><b>PRINCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.296">This letter doth make good the friar's words,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.297">Their course of love, the tidings of her death:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.298">And here he writes that he did buy a poison</a><br>
<a name="5.3.299">Of a poor 'pothecary, and therewithal</a><br>
<a name="5.3.300">Came to this vault to die, and lie with Juliet.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.301">Where be these enemies? Capulet! Montague!</a><br>
<a name="5.3.302">See, what a scourge is laid upon your hate,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.303">That heaven finds means to kill your joys with love.</a><br>
<a name="5.3.304">And I for winking at your discords too</a><br>
<a name="5.3.305">Have lost a brace of kinsmen: all are punish'd.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech62"><b>CAPULET</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.306">O brother Montague, give me thy hand:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.307">This is my daughter's jointure, for no more</a><br>
<a name="5.3.308">Can I demand.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech63"><b>MONTAGUE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.309">                  But I can give thee more:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.310">For I will raise her statue in pure gold;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.311">That while Verona by that name is known,</a><br>
<a name="5.3.312">There shall no figure at such rate be set</a><br>
<a name="5.3.313">As that of true and faithful Juliet.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech64"><b>CAPULET</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.314">As rich shall Romeo's by his lady's lie;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.315">Poor sacrifices of our enmity!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech65"><b>PRINCE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="5.3.316">A glooming peace this morning with it brings;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.317">The sun, for sorrow, will not show his head:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.318">Go hence, to have more talk of these sad things;</a><br>
<a name="5.3.319">Some shall be pardon'd, and some punished:</a><br>
<a name="5.3.320">For never was a story of more woe</a><br>
<a name="5.3.321">Than this of Juliet and her Romeo.</a><br>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>




</blockquote>
